Transport</a>)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n37,000<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right:0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height:1.35em;">\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.networkrail.co.uk/">www<wbr />.networkrail<wbr />.co<wbr />.uk</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Network Rail</b> is the owner (via its subsidiary Network Rail Infrastructure Ltd, which was known as Railtrack plc before 2002)<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Railway_infrastructure_manager" title="Railway infrastructure manager">infrastructure manager</a> of most of the railway network in <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Network Rail is an <a href="/wiki/Non-departmental_public_body" title="Non-departmental public body">arm\'s length public body</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> with no shareholders, which reinvests its income in the railways.\n</p><p>Network Rail\'s main customers are the private <a href="/wiki/Train_operating_company" title="Train operating company">train operating companies</a> (TOCs), responsible for passenger transport, and <a href="/wiki/Freight_operating_company" class="mw-redirect" title="Freight operating company">freight operating companies</a> (FOCs), who provide train services on the infrastructure that the company owns and maintains. Since 1 September 2014, Network Rail has been classified as a "public sector body".<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>To cope with <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Great_Britain_1995_to_date" title="History of rail transport in Great Britain 1995 to date">quickly rising passenger numbers</a>, Network Rail is currently undertaking a \xc2\xa338 billion <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Great_Britain_1995_to_date#Timeline" title="History of rail transport in Great Britain 1995 to date">programme of upgrades</a> to the network, including <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_in_Great_Britain" title="Railway electrification in Great Britain">electrification of lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_Programme" title="Thameslink Programme">upgrading Thameslink</a> and a new <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">high-speed line</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pre-2002">Pre-2002</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Pre-2002">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Rail transport in the United Kingdom">Britain\'s railway system</a> was built by private companies, but it was nationalised by the <a href="/wiki/Transport_Act_1947" title="Transport Act 1947">Transport Act 1947</a> and run by <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Railways</a> until <a href="/wiki/Privatisation_of_British_Rail" title="Privatisation of British Rail">re-privatisation</a> in the 1990s. Infrastructure, passenger and freight services were separated at that time. Between 1994 and 2002 the infrastructure was owned and operated by <a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a>.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Hatfield_train_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="Hatfield train crash">Hatfield train crash</a> on 17 October 2000 was a defining moment in the collapse of Railtrack.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The immediate major repairs undertaken across the whole British railway network were estimated to have cost in the order of <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">\xc2\xa3</a>580 million and Railtrack had no idea how many more \'Hatfields\' were waiting to happen because it had lost considerable in-house engineering skill following the sale or closure of many of the engineering and maintenance functions of <a href="/wiki/British_Rail" title="British Rail">British Rail</a> to external companies; nor did the company have any way of assessing the consequence of the speed restrictions it was ordering, which all but brought the railway network to a standstill.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The costs of modernising the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> were also spiralling.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, Railtrack announced that, despite making a pre-tax profit before exceptional expenses of \xc2\xa3199m, the \xc2\xa3733m of costs and compensation paid out over the Hatfield crash had plunged Railtrack from profit into a loss of \xc2\xa3534m,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> and it approached the government for funding, which it then used to pay a \xc2\xa3137m dividend to its shareholders in May 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Network Rail Ltd took over control by buying <a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a> plc, which was in "railway administration", from Railtrack Group plc for \xc2\xa3500 million; Railtrack plc was then renamed and reconstituted as Network Rail Infrastructure Ltd. The purchase was completed on 3 October 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The former company had thus never ceased to exist but continued under another name: for this reason Network Rail Infrastructure Ltd was the defendant in later prosecutions in respect of events which had occurred in the days of Railtrack.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2002_onwards">2002 onwards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2002 onwards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png/400px-UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png" width="400" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png/600px-UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png/800px-UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png 2x" data-file-width="1109" data-file-height="543" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:UK_total_rail_subsidies_1986-2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>UK total rail subsidies 1986\xe2\x80\x932015 (in 2015 terms), showing the huge increase after the Hatfield crash.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Following an initial period in which Network Rail established itself and demonstrated its competence in addressing the principal challenges of improving asset condition, reducing unit costs and tackling delay, the Government\'s Rail Review in 2004 said that Network Rail should be given responsibility for whole-industry performance reporting, timetable development, specification of small and medium network enhancements, and the delivery of route-specific utilisation strategies (RUS).<sup id="cite_ref-ORR-2005-06-Q4_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ORR-2005-06-Q4-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Some of these are functions which Network Rail already had; others \xe2\x80\x93 such as the obligation to devise <a href="/wiki/Route_Utilisation_Strategy" title="Route Utilisation Strategy">route utilisation strategies</a> \xe2\x80\x93 were transferred to Network Rail from the <a href="/wiki/Strategic_Rail_Authority" title="Strategic Rail Authority">Strategic Rail Authority</a>, a non-departmental public body, part of the UK government. The SRA was abolished in November 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The company moved its headquarters to Kings Place, 90 York Way, from 40 Melton Street, Euston, in August 2008. In October 2008, Sir <a href="/wiki/Ian_McAllister" title="Ian McAllister">Ian McAllister</a> announced that he would not stand for re-election as chairman of Network Rail. He had held the position for six years. He noted that as Network Rail moved to a "new phase in its development" it was appropriate for a new chairman to lead it there.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many track safety initiatives have been introduced in the time Network Rail has been responsible for this area. The latest, announced in December 2008, known as "All Orange", states that all track personnel must not only wear orange hi-vis waistcoats or jackets, but must also wear orange hi-vis trousers at all times when working on or near the track. This ruling came into force in January 2009 for maintenance and property workers and in April 2009 for infrastructure and investment sites.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Allegations_of_misuse_of_public_funds_and_discrimination">Allegations of misuse of public funds and discrimination</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Allegations of misuse of public funds and discrimination">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2009, allegations appeared in the media from the <a href="/wiki/Transport_Salaried_Staffs%27_Association" title="Transport Salaried Staffs&#39; Association">Transport Salaried Staffs\' Association</a> concerning treatment of Network Rail employees. Former chief executive <a href="/wiki/Iain_Coucher" title="Iain Coucher">Iain Coucher</a> was also accused of financial impropriety involving unspecified payments to his business partner Victoria Pender during his tenure at Network Rail.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-may_2011_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-may_2011-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An internal investigation held by Network Rail in 2010, vetted by its auditors <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PricewaterhouseCoopers</a>, uncovered no evidence of wrongdoing. An independent enquiry headed by Anthony White QC in 2011 further examined the claims, but also exonerated Coucher.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Knighthood_of_John_Armitt">Knighthood of John Armitt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Knighthood of John Armitt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Critical commentary appeared in the media concerning the <a href="/wiki/Knight_Bachelor" title="Knight Bachelor">knighthood</a> awarded to John Armitt in the <a href="/wiki/2012_New_Year_Honours" title="2012 New Year Honours">2012 New Year Honours</a> for services to engineering and construction. Armitt was Chief Executive of Network Rail at the time of the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Grayrigg_derailment" title="Grayrigg derailment">Grayrigg derailment</a> and the family of a victim of the accident criticised the award, which coincidentally was conferred on the same day that Network Rail were prosecuted for the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-knighthood_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-knighthood-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Regional_reorganisation">Regional reorganisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Regional reorganisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2011 the company began the process of reorganising its operational structure into nine semi-autonomous regional entities, each with their own managing director; the first two units to be created were Scotland and Wessex regions.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The reorganisation has been interpreted as a move back towards vertical integration of track and train operations.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flying_Scotsman_cancellation">Flying Scotsman cancellation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Flying Scotsman cancellation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2016 Network Rail failed to check whether the <i><a href="/wiki/LNER_Class_A3_4472_Flying_Scotsman" title="LNER Class A3 4472 Flying Scotsman">Flying Scotsman</a></i> could fit through tunnels along the Borders Route resulting in the cancellation of a trip just 24 hours before departure. The operator described the cancellation as "an absolute disgrace", Network Rail blamed the cancellation on an internal "administrative error"<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Just one day later Network Rail chose to change their mind and allow the train journey to take place. Scottish Transport Minister <a href="/wiki/Derek_Mackay" title="Derek Mackay">Derek Mackay</a> branded the affair a "debacle".<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Western_Electrification">Great Western Electrification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Great Western Electrification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Network Rail\'s attempt to electrify the <a href="/wiki/Great_Western_Main_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Western Main Line">Great Western Main Line</a> has been dogged by poor planning and cost overruns;<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> the projected cost had increased from \xc2\xa31.2 billion to \xc2\xa32.8 billion by the end of 2015<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and the project has been delayed to the point where the government has asked Hitachi to retrofit the new Intercity Express Programme trainsets with diesel as well as electric engines as the electrification has been scaled back.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sharing_of_responsibility_with_TOCs">Sharing of responsibility with TOCs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Sharing of responsibility with TOCs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In December 2016, the Transport Secretary, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Grayling" title="Chris Grayling">Chris Grayling</a> announced that Network Rail would lose sole control of track maintenance and repairs, and instead would share this with the Train Operating Companies.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Responsibilities">Responsibilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Responsibilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg/220px-Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg/330px-Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg/440px-Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Network_Rail_sign_at_Ledbury_railway_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sign showing the Network Rail name on the <a href="/wiki/Signal_box" class="mw-redirect" title="Signal box">signal box</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ledbury_railway_station" title="Ledbury railway station">Ledbury</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Network Rail owns the infrastructure, including the railway tracks, signals, overhead wires, tunnels, bridges, level crossings and most stations, but not the passenger or commercial freight rolling stock. It however owns a fleet of <a href="/wiki/Departmental_train" class="mw-redirect" title="Departmental train">departmental stock</a>.\n</p><p>Although it owns over 2,500 railway stations, it manages only 18 of the biggest and busiest of them, all the other stations being managed by one or other of the various train operating companies (TOCs).<sup id="cite_ref-networkrail.co.uk_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-networkrail.co.uk-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Network Rail has a 15-year lease on Square One in Manchester with 800 staff in one of Manchester\'s largest refurbished office spaces.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Network Rail should not be confused with \'<a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">National Rail</a>\'. National Rail is not an organisation, but merely a brand, used to explain and promote a Great Britain-wide network of passenger railway services. The majority of Network Rail lines also carry freight traffic; some lines are freight only. A few lines that carry passenger traffic are not part of the National Rail network (for example <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_1" title="High Speed 1">High Speed 1</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Express" title="Heathrow Express">Heathrow Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tyne_and_Wear_Metro" title="Tyne and Wear Metro">Tyne and Wear Metro</a> (the Tyne and Wear Metro uses Network Rail track between Pelaw and Sunderland and is responsible for that) and the <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a>). Conversely, a few National Rail services operate over track which is not part of the Network Rail network. For example, Chiltern Railways services run on track owned by London Underground between Harrow-on-the-Hill and Amersham.\n</p><p>The current Chairman is <a href="/wiki/Peter_Hendy" title="Peter Hendy">Sir Peter Hendy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mark_Carne" title="Mark Carne">Mark Carne</a> is currently appointed as the Chief Executive.<sup id="cite_ref-Our_Board_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Our_Board-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Funding">Funding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Funding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Financing_of_the_rail_industry_in_Great_Britain" title="Financing of the rail industry in Great Britain">Financing of the rail industry in Great Britain</a></div>\n<p>Network Rail is funded partly through a direct grant from the government (\xc2\xa33.8 billion in 2015/16) and partly by train operating companies paying access charges to use the rail network (\xc2\xa31.6 billion in 2015/16).  In 2015/16, it spent \xc2\xa33.1 billion on renewals (renewing existing infrastructure back to how it was when new) and \xc2\xa33.2 billion on enhancements, with the rest spent on maintenance and other costs.<sup id="cite_ref-1516gbrailfinance_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1516gbrailfinance-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Assets">Assets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Assets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Norwoodjunction4.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Norwoodjunction4.JPG/220px-Norwoodjunction4.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Norwoodjunction4.JPG/330px-Norwoodjunction4.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Norwoodjunction4.JPG/440px-Norwoodjunction4.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Norwoodjunction4.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Network Rail depot at <a href="/wiki/Norwood_Junction_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Norwood Junction station">Norwood Junction station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg/220px-2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg/330px-2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg/440px-2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1100" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2011_07_30_Unimog_bucket_truck_AE_05_ETK_of_Network_Rail_near_Kings_Cross_1300x1100.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Unimog" title="Unimog">Unimog</a> <a href="/wiki/Cherry_picker" class="mw-redirect" title="Cherry picker">bucket truck</a>.</div></div></div> \n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg/220px-Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg/330px-Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/94/Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg/440px-Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Taunton_66148_66116_railhead_treatment_train.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>High-pressure water jets clearing leaves at <a href="/wiki/Taunton_railway_station" title="Taunton railway station">Taunton</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Network Rail covers 20,000 miles of track, and 40,000 bridges and tunnels.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2003 Network Rail announced that it would take over all infrastructure maintenance work from private contractors, following concerns about the quality of work carried out by certain private firms, and spiralling costs.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>February 2004 saw the opening of an operations centre at <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">Waterloo station</a> in London, operated jointly by Network Rail and <a href="/wiki/South_West_Trains" title="South West Trains">South West Trains</a>. This was the first full collaboration of its kind since privatisation, and it is regarded as a model for other areas of the network, with a further six integrated Network Rail + TOC Control Centres having opened since then, at <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_station" title="Blackfriars station">Blackfriars</a>, <a href="/wiki/Croydon" title="Croydon">Croydon</a> (Leading Control for Thameslink), <a href="/wiki/Swindon_railway_station" title="Swindon railway station">Swindon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow</a> and, most recently, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">Liverpool Street</a> and South Wales based in Cardiff Canton.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Track renewal, the ongoing modernisation of the railway network by replacing track and signalling, continues to be carried out by private engineering firms under contract. The biggest renewals projects include the multibillion-pound upgrade of the London \xe2\x80\x93 Glasgow <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>, which was completed in 2008, the <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_Programme" title="Thameslink Programme">Thameslink Programme</a> to upgrade the north-south railway through London and work on the part of <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a> which is operated by Network Rail.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Network Rail initially sub-contracted much of the work and the site to private infrastructure maintenance companies such as <a href="/wiki/Carillion" title="Carillion">Carillion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Babcock_International_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Babcock International Group">First Engineering</a>. Other sub-contractors are used on site for specialist work or additional labour. These include Prima Services Group, Sky Blue, Balfour Beatty, Laboursite, BCL, Atkins (Atkins Rail) and McGinleys.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Since 2003 Network Rail has been building up significant in-house engineering skills, including funding of apprenticeship and foundation degree schemes. Network Rail reports significant savings resulting from the initial transfers of work away from contracting companies. Additional contracts were taken back by Network Rail after the serious <a href="/wiki/Potters_Bar_rail_crash" class="mw-redirect" title="Potters Bar rail crash">accident at Potters Bar</a> and other accidents at Rotherham and King\'s Cross led Jarvis to pull out of the track repair business. Shortly after this, and due to other failures by maintenance companies, Network Rail took control of many more maintenance duties. Telecomms maintenance came full circle in April 2009 with the bringing in house of the staff of Thales Telecom Services Ltd (formerly <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Telecommunications" title="British Rail Telecommunications">British Rail Telecommunications</a> (BRT)).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 2006, Network Rail made public a high-tech plan to combat the effects of <a href="/wiki/Slippery_rail" title="Slippery rail">slippery rail</a>. This plan involves the use of satellites for tracking trouble areas, water-jetting trains and crews using railhead scrubbers, sand sticks and a substance called Natrusolve, which dissolves leaf mulch.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All workers working on, near or trackside have to undergo a <a href="/wiki/Personal_Track_Safety" title="Personal Track Safety">Personal Track Safety</a> assessment (re-assessed every two years).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Network Rail workers undergo an assessment every year as part of AITL (Assessment in the Line). The AITL requires each worker to go through questions on a computer based program on all the competencies held.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In 2007 it was announced that the number of track renewal contractors will be reduced to four from the current six.\nThese are now <a href="/wiki/Amey_plc" title="Amey plc">Amey</a>/<a href="/wiki/Seco_Rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Seco Rail">SECO</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Beatty" title="Balfour Beatty">Balfour Beatty</a>, <a href="/wiki/Babcock_International_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="Babcock International Group">Babcock First Engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jarvis_plc" title="Jarvis plc">Jarvis plc</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Jarvis went into administration in March 2010,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> with the bulk of its work commitments being picked up by Babcock.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Stations">Stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Network Rail owns more than 2,500 railway stations, divided into <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_railway_station_categories" title="United Kingdom railway station categories">six categories</a>. Management and operation of most of them is carried out mostly by the principal <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_operating_trains_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of companies operating trains in the United Kingdom">train operating company</a> serving that station; however, in a few cases the train operating company does not serve the station. For example, <a href="/wiki/Hinckley_railway_station" title="Hinckley railway station">Hinckley</a> is served by <a href="/wiki/CrossCountry" title="CrossCountry">CrossCountry</a>, but it is managed by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Trains" title="East Midlands Trains">East Midlands Trains</a>. As of April 2018, Network Rail manages 20 stations directly, with Clapham Junction and Guildford becoming managed stations on 1 April 2018.  <sup id="cite_ref-networkrail.co.uk_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-networkrail.co.uk-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The stations Network Rail operate are:\n</p>\n<div>\n\n&#32;\n<table class="multicol" role="presentation" style="border-collapse: collapse; padding: 0; border: 0; background:transparent; width:100%;"><tbody><tr>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<p><b>National</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bristol_Temple_Meads_railway_station" title="Bristol Temple Meads railway station">Bristol Temple Meads</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Clapham_Junction_railway_station" title="Clapham Junction railway station">Clapham Junction</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh Waverley</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Guildford_railway_station" title="Guildford railway station">Guildford</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station">Liverpool Lime Street</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Reading_railway_station" title="Reading railway station">Reading</a></li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td>\n<td style="width: 50%;text-align: left; vertical-align: top;">\n<p><b>Central London stations</b>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/London_Bridge_station" title="London Bridge station">London Bridge</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Cannon_Street_station" title="Cannon Street station">London Cannon Street</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/London_Charing_Cross_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Charing Cross railway station">London Charing Cross</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/London_Euston_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Euston railway station">London Euston</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/London_King%27s_Cross_railway_station" title="London King&#39;s Cross railway station">London King\'s Cross</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Street_station" title="Liverpool Street station">London Liverpool Street</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/London_Paddington_station" title="London Paddington station">London Paddington</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/St_Pancras_station" class="mw-redirect" title="St Pancras station">London St Pancras</a> (but not the floor which is used for Eurostar services)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/London_Victoria_station" title="London Victoria station">London Victoria</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">London Waterloo</a></li></ul>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>Network Rail High Speed also operates <a href="/wiki/London_St_Pancras_International_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London St Pancras International railway station">London St Pancras International</a> High Level, <a href="/wiki/Stratford_International_station" title="Stratford International station">Stratford International</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ebbsfleet_International_railway_station" title="Ebbsfleet International railway station">Ebbsfleet International</a>. Glasgow Central and Liverpool Lime Street stations are divided into high and low-level stations \xe2\x80\x93 the high-level stations are all termini used primarily by the main inter-city services to those stations. The low-level stations are through routes on local commuter networks that are largely separate from other routes to the main station; these platforms are not managed by Network Rail, but instead the rail operator that primarily uses them (<a href="/wiki/Abellio_ScotRail" title="Abellio ScotRail">Abellio ScotRail</a> and <a href="/wiki/Merseyrail" title="Merseyrail">Merseyrail</a> respectively).\n</p><p>Network Rail operated <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport_railway_station" title="Gatwick Airport railway station">Gatwick Airport</a> station until January 2012 when it was transferred to <a href="/wiki/Southern_(train_operating_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern (train operating company)">Southern</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fenchurch_Street_railway_station" title="Fenchurch Street railway station">Fenchurch Street</a> until November 2014 when it was transferred to <a href="/wiki/C2c" title="C2c">c2c</a>. Network Rail took over management of Bristol Temple Meads and Reading in April 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A DfT franchise report in 2014 stated Network Rail\'s intention to subsume more major stations into Network Rail\'s directly operated portfolio. The report earmarked <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> for Network Rail management, as well as <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Manchester Oxford Road</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a> which are currently undergoing major rebuilding as part of the <a href="/wiki/Northern_Hub" title="Northern Hub">Northern Hub</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> However as of  September&#160;2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the two Manchester stations remain under the operatorship of <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Training_facilities">Training facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Training facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Network_Rail_30July06.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Network_Rail_30July06.JPG/220px-Network_Rail_30July06.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Network_Rail_30July06.JPG/330px-Network_Rail_30July06.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Network_Rail_30July06.JPG/440px-Network_Rail_30July06.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Network_Rail_30July06.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Network Rail\'s Coventry leadership development centre, Westwood.</div></div></div>\n<p>Network Rail has several training and development sites around Britain. These include sites in <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_upon_Tyne" title="Newcastle upon Tyne">Newcastle</a>, Peterborough, Derby, Leeds, <a href="/wiki/Walsall" title="Walsall">Walsall</a> and <a href="/wiki/Larbert" title="Larbert">Larbert</a> which provide refresher courses, and train staff in new equipment. Advanced Apprentice Scheme trainees are trained at Network Rail\'s Westwood training centre for the first five months of their apprenticeship and then are trained further at <a href="/wiki/HMS_Sultan_(establishment)" title="HMS Sultan (establishment)">HMS <i>Sultan</i></a> in Gosport over seven 2-week periods or five 3-week periods (throughout their second and third year) of their apprenticeship, using a combination of <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a> facilities and a specially installed training centre. All courses are taught by VT Flagship (part of <a href="/wiki/Babcock_International" title="Babcock International">Babcock International</a>) in the first year but apprentices are trained by Network Rail staff in the second and third years.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Network Rail bought a residential centre from <a href="/wiki/Cable_%26_Wireless_plc" title="Cable &amp; Wireless plc">Cable and Wireless</a> in the Westwood Business Centre near <a href="/wiki/Coventry" title="Coventry">Coventry</a> for leadership development. The company and other industry partners such as <a href="/wiki/VolkerRail" title="VolkerRail">VolkerRail</a> and Balfour Beatty also operate a Foundation Degree in conjunction with Sheffield Hallam University.\n</p><p>In 2008, Network Rail piloted its first qualification in "track engineering". It has been given permission to develop courses equivalent to GCSE and A-levels.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Telecoms_assets">Telecoms assets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Telecoms assets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Network Rail operates various essential telecommunication circuits for signalling and electrification control systems, train radio systems, lineside communications, level crossing CCTV, station information and security systems as well as more general IT and business telephony needs. The fixed bearer network infrastructure comprises transmission systems and telephone exchanges linked by a fibre optic and copper cable network that is located mainly within trackside troughing routes on the former <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Telecommunications" title="British Rail Telecommunications">British Rail Telecommunications</a> network. (It is the largest private telecoms network in the UK).\n</p><p>Network Rail operates several analogue radio networks that support mobile communication applications for drivers and lineside workers which consist of base stations, antenna systems and control equipment. The National Radio Network (NRN) was developed specifically for the operational railway; it provides radio coverage for 98% of the rail network through 500 base stations and 21 radio exchanges. The Radio Electronic Token Block <a href="/wiki/RETB" class="mw-redirect" title="RETB">RETB</a> system is based on similar technology as the NRN and ORN but provides data communication for signalling token exchange as well as voice communication.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Fixed communication at trackside is provided by telephone. These are primarily provided for signallers to communicate with train crew, via telephones mounted on signal posts, and with the public through telephones located at level crossings.\nGAI-Tronics provides many of the telephones sited on trackside and at level crossings. They also provide Public Access Help Points on platforms and stations to provide passengers with easy access to Information and Emergency control centres.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/GSM-R" title="GSM-R">GSM-R</a> radio systems are being introduced across <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a> under <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">EU</a> legislation for interoperability. In the UK, as of March 2014, Network Rail is well underway in the UK implementation of GSM-R to replace its legacy National Radio Network (NRN) and Cab Secure Radio (CSR) systems currently in use.\n</p><p>Network Rail has an internal infrastructure database known as GEOGIS. The system uses codes for four-digit Track IDs to identify which line at any location is referred to. The first number refers to track direction, with values of 1 (Up), 2 (Down), 3 (Reversible/Bi-directional), or 4 (Merry Go Round Loop). The second number refers to track use, which can be 1 (Main or Fast), 2 (Slow, Local or Relief), 3 (Goods), 4 (Single line), 5 (Loop), 6 (Terminal or Bay), 7 (Crossover), 8 (Other or Engine), or 9 (Single Siding). The third and fourth numbers refer to the track number, which can be any number from 00 to 99 inclusive, and are usually numbered sequentially.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rolling_stock">Rolling stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Rolling stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Network Rail operates a large variety of DMUs, locomotives and rolling stock to perform safety checks and maintenance (this fleet is not to be confused with the combined rolling stock assets of <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Train_Operating_Companies" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Train Operating Companies">ATOC</a> members who work in combination as <i><a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">National Rail</a></i>). As well as the multiple units and locomotives detailed below, Network Rail own and operate a large stock of rolling stock for particular testing duties and track maintenance. Network Rail also hire freight locomotives from various freight operators including <a href="/wiki/DB_Cargo_UK" title="DB Cargo UK">DB Cargo UK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Freightliner_UK" class="mw-redirect" title="Freightliner UK">Freightliner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colas_Rail" title="Colas Rail">Colas Rail</a> and <a href="/wiki/GB_Railfreight" title="GB Railfreight">GB Railfreight</a> amongst others to operate engineers\' trains in support of maintenance and renewal work. Network Rail\'s Infrastructure Monitoring fleet of test trains is operated by Colas Rail, primarily using locomotives from Colas\' and Network Rail\'s own fleets, but also using locomotives hired from other companies such as <a href="/wiki/Direct_Rail_Services" title="Direct Rail Services">Direct Rail Services</a>, GB Railfreight and <a href="/wiki/Europhoenix" title="Europhoenix">Europhoenix</a> as required.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th align="left">Class\n</th>\n<th align="left">Image\n</th>\n<th align="left">Type\n</th>\n<th align="left">Introduced\n</th>\n<th in 1983)</i>\n</td>\n<td align="center">3\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_asset_sales">Possible asset sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Possible asset sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In May 2015, it was reported in the national press that the government was considering selling off some of Network Rail\'s assets, including large stations and <a href="/wiki/Wi-fi" class="mw-redirect" title="Wi-fi">wi-fi</a> services. The government denied the reports.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_investment_programme">Current investment programme</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Current investment programme">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Great_Britain_1995_to_date#Timeline" title="History of rail transport in Great Britain 1995 to date">Timeline of future railway upgrades in Britain</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:362px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png/360px-GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png" width="360" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png/540px-GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png/720px-GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png 2x" data-file-width="1079" data-file-height="649" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GBR_rail_passengers_by_year_1830-2015.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Rail Passengers in Great Britain from 1829-2016, showing the early era of small railway companies, the amalgamation into the "Big Four", nationalisation and finally the current era of privatisation.</div></div></div>\n<p>From 1997 to 2014 (inclusive), passenger numbers have more than doubled, following little growth in the previous decades. To cope with the increasing passenger numbers, Network Rail is currently undertaking a \xc2\xa338 billion <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Great_Britain_1995_to_date#Timeline" title="History of rail transport in Great Britain 1995 to date">programme of upgrades</a> to the network, including <a href="/wiki/Crossrail" title="Crossrail">Crossrail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_in_Great_Britain" title="Railway electrification in Great Britain">electrification of lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Rail_Traffic_Management_System_in_Great_Britain" title="European Rail Traffic Management System in Great Britain">in-cab signalling</a>, new <a href="/wiki/Intercity_Express_Programme" title="Intercity Express Programme">inter-city trains</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thameslink_Programme" title="Thameslink Programme">upgrading Thameslink</a>, and a new <a href="/wiki/HS2" class="mw-redirect" title="HS2">high-speed line</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_GRIP_process">The GRIP process</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: The GRIP process">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>For investment projects, as opposed to routine maintenance, Network Rail has developed an eight-stage process designed to minimise and mitigate risks. This is known as the Governance for Railway Investment Projects (GRIP), previously known as \xe2\x80\x9cGuide to Rail Investment Projects\xe2\x80\x9d.<sup id="cite_ref-GRIP_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GRIP-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The stages are as follows:\n</p>\n<ol><li>output definition;</li>\n<li>pre-feasibility;</li>\n<li>option selection;</li>\n<li>single option development;</li>\n<li>detailed design;</li>\n<li>construction, test and commission;</li>\n<li>scheme hand back;</li>\n<li>project close out.</li></ol>\n<p>Each stage delivers an agreed set of outputs to defined quality criteria.<sup id="cite_ref-GRIP_54-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GRIP-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_periods">Control periods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Control periods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail_Control_Periods" title="Network Rail Control Periods">Network Rail Control Periods</a></div>\n<p>For financial and other planning purposes, Network Rail works within 5-year "Control Periods", each one beginning on 1 April and ending on 31 March to coincide with the financial reporting year. These periods were inherited from Railtrack, so that the earlier ones are retrospective, and not necessarily of 5 years duration. They are as follows:\n</p>\n<ul><li>Control Period 1 (CP1): 1996\xe2\x80\x932001</li>\n<li>Control Period 2 (CP2): 2001\xe2\x80\x932004</li>\n<li>Control Period 3 (CP3): 2004\xe2\x80\x932009</li>\n<li>Control Period 4 (CP4): 2009\xe2\x80\x932014</li>\n<li>Control Period 5 (CP5): 2014\xe2\x80\x932019</li>\n<li>Control Period 6 (CP6): 2019\xe2\x80\x932024</li>\n<li>Control Period 7 (CP7): 2024\xe2\x80\x932029</li>\n<li>Control Period 8 (CP8): 2029\xe2\x80\x932034</li></ul>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a> regularly issues a <i>High-Level Output Specification</i> (HLOS) indicating what work the Government wishes to be undertaken during a given Control Period.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Route_plans">Route plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Route plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg/350px-Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg.png" width="350" height="425" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg/525px-Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg/700px-Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1108" data-file-height="1345" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_of_Network_Rail_Strategic_Routes_in_England_and_Wales_2014.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Strategic Routes in England and Wales 2014.</div></div></div>\n<p>Network Rail regularly publishes a Strategic Business Plan detailing their policies, processes and plans, as well as financial expenditure and other data. The most recent complete business plan was published in January 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-NRBP2014_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRBP2014-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Within these plans the rail network is divided into ten \xe2\x80\x9cdevolved routes\xe2\x80\x9d or \xe2\x80\x9coperational routes\xe2\x80\x9d, with a Route Plan for each being published annually.<sup id="cite_ref-NRBP2014_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRBP2014-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\nEach route or other plan covers a number of railway lines usually defined by geographical area and the routes are further subdivided into 17 \xe2\x80\x9cstrategic routes\xe2\x80\x9d, each divided into Strategic Route Sections (SRS) and given an SRS number and name.<sup id="cite_ref-NRNRS_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRNRS-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The plans also detail the geography of routes, stations, major junctions, capacity constraints and other issues and provide data on <a href="/wiki/Loading_gauge#Great_Britain" title="Loading gauge">freight gauge</a>, <a href="/wiki/Railway_electrification_system" title="Railway electrification system">electrification</a>, line speed, number of tracks, capacity and other information. The plans also detail the expected future demand and development of each route, their predicted expenditure and their maintenance and investment requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-NRRPI_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRRPI-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The devolved routes were introduced in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-NRNSA_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRNSA-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> and the 17 strategic routes labelled "A" to "Q" were introduced in 2010. From 2004 to 2009, the network had been divided into 26 strategic routes numbered "1" to "26". In 2003, the network had been divided into 41 strategic routes numbered "1" to "41".<sup id="cite_ref-NRRPA_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRRPA-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 2011 devolved routes and strategic routes are organised as in the table below.<sup id="cite_ref-NRNRS_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NRNRS-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table West Coast Main Line</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>O\n</td>\n<td style="background-color:#fad600;">\n</td>\n<td>Merseyside\n</td>\n<td><i>none</i>\n</td>\n<td><span style="font-size:85%;"><div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chester_railway_station" title="Chester railway station"> Chester</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ellesmere_Port_railway_station" title="Ellesmere Port railway station"> Ellesmere Port</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kirkby_railway_station" title="Kirkby railway station"> Kirkby</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Central_railway_station" title="Liverpool Central railway station"> Liverpool Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station" title="Liverpool Lime Street railway station"> Liverpool Lime Street</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Liverpool_South_Parkway_railway_station" title="Liverpool South Parkway railway station"> Liverpool South Parkway</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/New_Brighton_railway_station" title="New Brighton railway station"> New Brighton</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ormskirk_railway_station" title="Ormskirk railway station"> Ormskirk</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Southport_railway_station" title="Southport railway station"> Southport</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/West_Kirby_railway_station" title="West Kirby railway station"> West Kirby</a></li></ul>\n</div></span>\n</td>\n<td><span style="font-size:85%;">21. Merseyrail</span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="2">Scotland\n</td>\n<td>P\n</td>\n<td style="background-color:#ff7f00;">\n</td>\n<td>Scotland East\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station"> Edinburgh Waverley</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Carstairs_railway_station" title="Carstairs railway station"> Carstairs</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Falkirk_High_railway_station" title="Falkirk High railway station"> Falkirk High</a>\n</td>\n<td><span style="font-size:85%;"><div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_railway_station" title="Aberdeen railway station"> Aberdeen</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dundee_railway_station" title="Dundee railway station"> Dundee</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Queen_Street_railway_station" title="Glasgow Queen Street railway station"> Glasgow Queen Street</a> High Level</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Inverness_railway_station" title="Inverness railway station"> Inverness</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kyle_of_Lochalsh_railway_station" title="Kyle of Lochalsh railway station"> Kyle of Lochalsh</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stirling_railway_station,_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Stirling railway station, Scotland">Stirling</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Thurso_railway_station" title="Thurso railway station"> Thurso</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Wick_railway_station" title="Wick railway station"> Wick</a></li></ul>\n</div></span>\n</td>\n<td><span style="font-size:85%;"><div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>24. Highlands (part)</li></ul>\n</div></span>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Q\n</td>\n<td style="background-color:#e719ca;">\n</td>\n<td>Scotland West\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Carstairs_railway_station" title="Carstairs railway station"> Carstairs</a> \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Glasgow Central railway station"> Glasgow Central</a>\n</td>\n<td><span style="font-size:85%;"><div class="hlist">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ardrossan_Harbour_railway_station" title="Ardrossan Harbour railway station"> Ardrossan Harbour</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Ayr_railway_station" title="Ayr railway station"> Ayr</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dumbarton_Central_railway_station" title="Dumbarton Central railway station"> Dumbarton Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dumfries_railway_station" title="Dumfries railway station"> Dumfries</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Fort_William_railway_station" title="Fort William railway station"> Fort William</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Queen_Street_railway_station" title="Glasgow Queen Street railway station"> Glasgow Queen Street</a> Low Level</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Greenock_Central_railway_station" title="Greenock Central railway station"> Greenock Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Helensburgh_Central_railway_station" title="Helensburgh Central railway station"> Helensburgh Central</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Largs_railway_station" title="Largs railway station"> Largs</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Mallaig_railway_station" title="Mallaig railway station"> Mallaig</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Oban_railway_station" title="Oban railway station"> Oban</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Stranraer_railway_station" title="Stranraer railway station"> Stranraer</a></li></ul>\n</div></span>\n</td>\n<td><span style="font-size:85%;"><div class="plainlist">\n<ul><li>25. Highlands (part)</li>\n<li>26. Strathclyde and South West Scotland</li></ul>\n</div></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Electricity">Electricity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Electricity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Network Rail opened the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Solar_power_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Solar power in the United Kingdom">solar-powered bridge</a> at Blackfriars Bridge across the <a href="/wiki/River_Thames" title="River Thames">River Thames</a> in January 2014. The roof of the bridge has been covered with 4,400 <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_panels" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic panels">photovoltaic panels</a>, providing up to half of the energy for London <a href="/wiki/Blackfriars_station" title="Blackfriars station">Blackfriars station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_structure_and_accountability">Governance structure and accountability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Governance structure and accountability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_governance_structure">Formal governance structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Formal governance structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The company is accountable to a body of members through its corporate constitution,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> to its commercial train operator customers through its contracts with them (the contracts are subject to regulatory oversight), and to the public interest through the statutory powers of the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Rail_and_Road" title="Office of Rail and Road">Office of Rail and Road</a> (ORR).<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since Network Rail does not have shareholders, its members hold the board of directors to account for their management of the business. From 1 July 2015 all the members were removed leaving the special member, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Secretary of State for Transport</a>, as the sole member of Network Rail.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Previously at any one time there were around 100 members in total, drawn from a wide range of industry partners and members of the public. There were two general categories of membership, industry members comprising any organisation holding a licence to operate on the railway or preferred bidder for a railway franchise, and public members who were drawn from the wider stakeholder community. Members were appointed by an independent panel and served a three-year term. They had a number of statutory rights and duties which included attending annual general meetings, receiving the Annual Report and Accounts, and approving the appointment or re-appointment of Network Rail\xe2\x80\x99s directors. Members had a duty to act in the best interests of the company without personal bias. They received no payments other than travel expenses.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Setting the strategic direction and the day-to-day management of Network Rail is the responsibility of the company\xe2\x80\x99s board of directors. That direction must be consistent with the regulatory jurisdiction of the ORR, and with the requirements of its contracts. The ORR in turn operates within the overall transport policy set by the UK <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Transport" title="Department for Transport">Department for Transport</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish government">Scottish government</a>, including as to what the government wants the railway industry to achieve and how much money the government is prepared to put into the industry. This means that the degree of government influence and control over the company is higher than it was before these enlargements of the powers and role of the government were introduced by the <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_2005" title="Railways Act 2005">Railways Act 2005</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Monitoring_Network_Rail.27s_performance"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Monitoring_Network_Rail\'s_performance">Monitoring Network Rail\'s performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Monitoring Network Rail&#039;s performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Rail_and_Road" title="Office of Rail and Road">Office of Rail and Road</a> (ORR) monitors Network Rail\'s performance on a continuous basis against targets established by the regulatory authority in the most recent access charges review (2003), against obligations in the company\'s network licence and against forecasts in its own business plan. If performance is poor, the company will face criticism and possible enforcement action from its commercial customers (under their contracts) and from the ORR (enforcing the company\'s network licence). It may also be criticised by its members in general meeting.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>In the annual report 2014/15, the ORR reported that the <a href="/wiki/Public_Performance_Measure" title="Public Performance Measure">Public Performance Measure</a> (PPM) was 89.6%, 1.4 percentage points (pp) below target in England and Wales, and PPM in Scotland was 90.5%, 1.5pp below its regulatory performance target of 92%.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Informal_governance_groups">Informal governance groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Informal governance groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="Railway_Industry_Planning_Group_.28RIPG.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Railway_Industry_Planning_Group_(RIPG)">Railway Industry Planning Group (RIPG)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Railway Industry Planning Group (RIPG)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Railway Industry Planning Group (RIPG), chaired by Network Rail, has as its purpose railway industry input into the structure and development of the national railway strategic planning processes. Its members are drawn from railway funders, operators and users,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> and the group meets quarterly to consider:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>rail industry liaison with regional and local government</li>\n<li>Regional (and Scotland and Wales) Planning Assessments</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Route_Utilisation_Strategy" title="Route Utilisation Strategy">Route Utilisation Strategies</a></li>\n<li>specification of passenger operator franchises</li>\n<li>High Level Output Specifications and Network Rail\xe2\x80\x99s Strategic Business Plan</li>\n<li>Network Rail\xe2\x80\x99s Business Planning Criteria, Business Plan and Route Plans.</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Directors">Directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
