(businessman)">Sir David Higgins</a></td>\n<td>Now running HS2\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>&#32;\n</p>\n</td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p><br />\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Safety">Safety</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Safety">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png/330px-Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png" width="330" height="202" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png/495px-Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png/660px-Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png 2x" data-file-width="736" data-file-height="451" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rail_fatalities_of_European_countries.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2013 Rail fatalities per billion passenger-km in European countries.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>While generally strong, the safety record of the company was marred in February 2007 when a Virgin express <a href="/wiki/Grayrigg_derailment" title="Grayrigg derailment">derailed at Grayrigg</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cumbria" title="Cumbria">Cumbria</a>. Network Rail admitted responsibility for the incident. The <a href="/wiki/Rail_Accident_Investigation_Branch" title="Rail Accident Investigation Branch">RAIB</a> investigation concluded in 2009 that a faulty set of points had caused the derailment.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Rail_Regulation" class="mw-redirect" title="Office of Rail Regulation">Office of Rail Regulation</a> announced that Network Rail was to be prosecuted under the <a href="/wiki/Health_and_Safety_at_Work_Act_1974" class="mw-redirect" title="Health and Safety at Work Act 1974">Health and Safety Act</a> for "failure to provide and implement suitable and sufficient standards, procedures, guidance, training, tools and resources for the inspection and maintenance of fixed stretcher bar points".  Network Rail pleaded guilty and were fined \xc2\xa34.1 million including legal costs.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC16544694_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC16544694-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2005 two young girls were killed by a train as they were crossing the railway line via a pedestrian <a href="/wiki/Level_crossing" title="Level crossing">level crossing</a> at <a href="/wiki/Elsenham_railway_station" title="Elsenham railway station">Elsenham</a> in Essex. Network Rail was prosecuted for breaching <a href="/wiki/Health_and_safety" class="mw-redirect" title="Health and safety">health and safety</a> law and fined \xc2\xa31 million in March 2012. The court heard that risk assessments carried out by Network Rail staff in 2002 had identified potential dangers with the crossing and recommended the installation of gates that would lock automatically as trains approached, but this was not acted upon.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc-elsenham_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc-elsenham-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Private_versus_public-sector_status">Private versus public-sector status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Private versus public-sector status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a></div>\n<p>In 2001 the then Labour government denied that it had nationalised the rail network in order to prevent Railtrack\'s shareholders claiming, via the European Court of Human Rights, the four-year average price of Railtrack, about \xc2\xa310 per share. Instead, Railtrack\'s shareholders were given only \xc2\xa32.60.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Times</i> reported that Gordon Brown\'s aide, <a href="/wiki/Shriti_Vadera,_Baroness_Vadera" title="Shriti Vadera, Baroness Vadera">Shriti Vadera</a> e-mailed <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Byers" title="Stephen Byers">Stephen Byers</a> in July 2001 asking: "Can we engineer the solution through insolvency ... and therefore avoid <a href="/wiki/Compensation_(nationalization)" class="mw-redirect" title="Compensation (nationalization)">compensation</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Act_1998" title="Human Rights Act 1998">Human Rights Act</a>?"<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Railtrack" title="Railtrack">Railtrack</a> plc was placed into railway administration under the <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_1993" title="Railways Act 1993">Railways Act 1993</a> on 7 October 2001, following an application to the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Justice_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="High Court of Justice of England and Wales">High Court</a> by the then <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_Transport" title="Secretary of State for Transport">Transport Secretary</a>, Stephen Byers.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> It was reported in November 2001 that a further \xc2\xa33.5 billion might be needed to keep the national railway network running, a sum disputed by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_%26_Young" title="Ernst &amp; Young">Ernst &amp; Young</a>, the administrators.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> To get Railtrack out of administration, the government had to go back to the High Court and present evidence that the company was no longer insolvent. The principal reason given by the government to the court for this assertion was the decision of the <a href="/wiki/Rail_Regulator" title="Rail Regulator">rail regulator</a> in 2002 to carry out an interim review of the company\'s finances, with the potential to advance significant additional sums to the company.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The High Court accepted that the company was not insolvent, and the railway administration order was discharged in October 2002.\n</p><p>Until 2013, there was discussion over whether Network Rail is a public-sector or a private-sector entity. Although it was officially a private sector organisation, the fact that its debts were underwritten by the government, and it is partially funded by the government, has led to its being described as being "nationalisation in all but name".<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> It was also claimed that the government is keen for Network Rail not to be classified as a public-sector organisation, as this would mean that the company\'s debt would be counted as public expenditure liabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian2013-12-17_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2013-12-17-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Office_for_National_Statistics" title="Office for National Statistics">Office for National Statistics</a> (ONS) repeatedly clashed with the <a href="/wiki/National_Audit_Office_(United_Kingdom)" title="National Audit Office (United Kingdom)">National Audit Office</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Statistics_Commission" title="Statistics Commission">Statistics Commission</a> over whether the successor to Railtrack should be considered a private company \xe2\x80\x93 as the ONS believed \xe2\x80\x93 or included on the Government\'s books, as the National Audit Office argued. The NAO said that as the Government is bearing the risk that would normally be borne by equity capital, and as it can appoint, through the SRA, a director who cannot be removed by members, Network Rail is effectively a subsidiary of the Government-controlled SRA.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2013, the ONS announced that from September 2014, Network Rail will be classified as a "government body". This resulted in the company\'s debt of \xc2\xa334 billion being added to the <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">national debt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian2013-12-17_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2013-12-17-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="National_Centre">National Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: National Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Quadrant:MK" title="Quadrant:MK">Quadrant:MK</a></div>\n<p>The new national centre now known as \'The Quadrant:MK\' is in <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes" title="Milton Keynes">Milton Keynes</a>: it completed construction in June 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The complex is five minutes\' walk from <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">Milton Keynes Central</a>. The four buildings, which are connected to a central street, accommodate about 3,000 people. As of  June 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the engineering, logistics, operations including timetable planning, IT, procurement, planning and finance departments all planned to move to the Quadrant.<sup id="cite_ref-rg_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rg-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Photography_competition">Photography competition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Photography competition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Network Rail organises the Landscape Photographer of the Year competition. Shortlisted photos are displayed at <a href="/wiki/London_Waterloo_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Waterloo railway station">London Waterloo</a> and other major stations.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Network_Rail&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Northern_Ireland_Railways" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Ireland Railways">Northern Ireland Railways</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Financing_of_the_rail_industry_in_Great_Britain" title="Financing of the rail industry in Great Britain">Financing of the rail industry in Great Britain</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span
